## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / mathematical biology (population growth ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target is a time-derivative dP_dt driven by current population size P (and possibly explicit time forcing t), which is the standard setting for continuous-time population dynamics. Typical relationships include per-capita growth proportional to P, density dependence via nonlinear (often polynomial or rational) functions of P, and time-varying growth/harvest terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Time-varying exponential growth: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (slow trend in intrinsic rate)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (crowding reduces growth; c1 ~ 1/K)
- Higher-order density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P**3 (stronger-than-quadratic crowding effects)
- Theta-logistic (generalized crowding): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible curvature of density dependence)
- Gompertz-type growth (log-density dependence): dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth decreases with log(P))
- Allee effect (strong Allee with carrying capacity): dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (negative growth at low P; saturation at high P)
- Weak Allee effect (smooth boost at low P): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * P**2 (enhanced growth at intermediate densities)
- Saturating per-capita birth with linear death: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (birth saturates with P; constant per-capita mortality)
- Saturating total growth (Holling-II on P): dP_dt = c0 * P / (P + c1) - c2 * P (limited recruitment/space; density-dependent via saturation)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 (removal independent of P; can create extinction threshold)
- Proportional harvesting (effort-based): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P (additional per-capita loss term)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P - c4 * P**2 (periodic environment modulates intrinsic growth)
- Time-varying carrying capacity proxy: dP_dt = c0 * P - (c1 + c2 * exp(-c3 * t)) * P**2 (density dependence relaxes/strengthens over time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-independent growth corresponds to dP_dt proportional to P, so the per-capita rate (dP_dt / P) is approximately constant.
- Crowding/competition is often represented by negative curvature in P (e.g., -P**2, -P**3, or -(P**theta)), producing a peak in dP_dt at intermediate P.
- Allee effects require a sign change in per-capita growth at low P; structurally this appears as an extra factor like (c*P - 1) multiplying P and the crowding term.
- Gompertz-like regulation is suggested when the per-capita growth rate depends roughly linearly on log(P), i.e., (dP_dt / P) ~ a - b*log(P).
- Saturating recruitment/limited resources often yield rational forms in P (e.g., P/(1+cP) or P/(P+c)), reflecting diminishing returns at high density.
- Harvesting or external mortality appears as subtractive terms independent of P (constant yield) or proportional to P (effort-based), shifting equilibria and enabling extinction thresholds.
- Seasonal/environmental forcing is indicated by periodic dependence on t (sin/cos in coefficients), causing oscillatory growth rate even without explicit population cycles.
- Time-dependent habitat quality/capacity is represented by coefficients that vary with t (e.g., exponential relaxation), effectively making the strength of density dependence change over time.
